# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Kafka

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle: the Lifecycle interface (or equivalent), the service startup ordering, and the coordinated shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

60-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the research on Apache Kafka's service lifecycle management pattern and created the `answer.json` file with comprehensive findings.

## Summary of Findings

I identified the **Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle pattern** in Apache Kafka across two major areas:

### **Scala-based Server Infrastructure** 
The core lifecycle is defined by the **Server trait** (in `kafka/server/Server.scala`) with three methods:
- `startup()` - initiate startup
- `shutdown()` - initiate shutdown  
- `awaitShutdown()` - wait for completion

**KafkaRaftServer** orchestrates dependent services with proper startup/shutdown ordering:
- **Startup**: Controller first, then Broker
- **Shutdown**: Broker first (reverse order), then Controller

### **Detailed Implementation in BrokerServer**
The **BrokerServer** contains an extensive lifecycle with components started in dependency order and stopped in reverse order, including:
- Scheduler, Log Manager, Socket Server
- Replica Manager, Coordinators (group, transaction, share)
- Various managers and metadata publishers

### **Connect Framework Pattern**
The **Herder interface** and **AbstractHerder** class implement coordinated startup/shutdown of dependent services:
- **startServices()**: Worker → StatusBackingStore → ConfigBackingStore
- **stopServices()**: StatusBackingStore → ConfigBackingStore → Worker (reverse order)

### **Key Patterns**
1. ✅ Dependent services start after dependencies, stop before them
2. ✅ State machine (SHUTDOWN → STARTING → STARTED → SHUTTING_DOWN)
3. ✅ Reverse-order shutdown ensures invariants are maintained
4. ✅ Fault-tolerant cleanup (failures don't cascade)
5. ✅ Future-based coordination for async milestones

The answer file contains 10 key files and 9 core symbols that implement this comprehen

\n108: /**\n109:  * Abstract Herder implementation which handles connector/task lifecycle tracking. Extensions\n110:  * must invoke the lifecycle hooks appropriately.\n111:  * <p>\n112:  * This class takes the following approach for sending status updates to the backing store:\n113:  *\n114:  * <ol>\n115:  * <li>\n116:  *    When the connector or task is starting, we overwrite the previous state blindly. This ensures that\n117:  *    every rebalance will reset the state of tasks to the proper state. The intuition is that there should\n118:  *    be less chance of write conflicts when the worker has just received its assignment and is starting tasks.\n119:  *    In particular, this prevents us from depending on the generation absolutely. If the group disappears\n120:  *    and the generation is reset, then we'll overwrite the status information with the older (and larger)\n121:  *    generation with the updated one. The danger of this approach is that slow starting tasks may cause the\n122:  *    status to be overwritten after a rebalance has completed.\n123:  *\n124:  * <li>\n125:  *    If the connector or task fails or is shutdown, we use {@link StatusBackingStore#putSafe(ConnectorStatus)},\n126:  *    which provides a little more protection if the worker is no longer in the group (in which case the\n127:  *    task may have already been started on another worker). Obviously this is still racy. If the task has just\n128:  *    started on another worker, we may not have the updated status cached yet. In this case, we'll overwrite\n129:  *    the value which will cause the state to be inconsistent (most likely until the next rebalance). Until\n130:  *    we have proper producer groups with fenced groups, there is not much else we can do.\n131:  * </ol>\n132:  */\n133: public abstract class AbstractHerder implements Herder, connectorClientConfigOverridePolicy,\n156:                           Time time) {\n157:         this.worker = worker;\n158:         this.worker.herder = this;\n159:         this.workerId = workerId;\n160:         this.kafkaClusterId = kafkaClusterId;\n161:         this.statusBackingStore = statusBackingStore;\n162:         this.configBackingStore = configBackingStore;\n163:         this.connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin = Plugin.wrapInstance(\n164:                 connectorClientConfigOverridePolicy,\n165:                 worker.metrics().metrics(),\n166:                 WorkerConfig.CONNECTOR_CLIENT_POLICY_CLASS_CONFIG);\n167:         this.connectorExecutor = Executors.newCachedThreadPool();\n168:         this.time = time;\n169:         this.loggers = order\\n\\n## Key Lifecycle Patterns\\n\\n1. **Dependent Service Ordering**: Services with dependencies start after their dependencies and stop before them\\n2. **Status State Machine**: Explicit state transitions prevent invalid operations and enable monitoring\\n3. **Reverse-Order Shutdown**: Shutdown sequence reverses startup sequence to maintain invariants\\n4. **Fault-Tolerant Cleanup**: CoreUtils.swallow() ensures one failure doesn't prevent other shutdown tasks\\n5. **Future-Based Coordination**: CompletableFuture enables waiting for asynchronous startup/shutdown milestones\\n6.
